RT @civilrightsorg: Thank you @SenKamalaHarris, Sen. @CoryBooker, and @SenatorTimScott. This legislation is deeply important and has been a‚Ä¶
Remember: Civil rights work, including the fight for meaningful justice reform, has never been easy. We won't always get the *perfect* piece of reform legislation. But we can‚Äôt win if we don‚Äôt fight.		And @civilrightsorg is committed to being in that fight for the long haul.
.@civilrightsorg will continue to advocate for meaningful justice reform in the future, because the #FirstStepAct is truly just the beginning. Congress has much more work to do to achieve the transformational change that will end mass incarceration in America. So do we.
#FirstStepAct continues to exclude people from benefiting from some provisions based solely on their prior offenses, namely citizenship &amp; immigration status, as well as certain prior drug convictions and their "risk score" as determined by a discriminatory risk assessment system.
But #FirstStepAct falls short in many ways. Several sentencing provisions don't apply to people currently incarcerated and it excludes too many people from earning time credits. Troublingly, it also allows private prison companies to profit &amp; fails to include parole for children.
The #FirstStepAct would revise mandatory minimum sentences for certain drug offenses, including finally making retroactive the 2010 Fair Sentencing Act that reduced the crack-powder sentencing disparity. And it would fix the ‚Äògood time‚Äô credit calculation. That's critical.
Over the past several months, @civilrightsorg has worked closely with Senate offices and our coalition members to reach commonsense solutions that promote justice and fairness across the system ‚Äì and the #FirstStepAct now offers some important improvements.
When the House passed the original #FirstStepAct in May, @civilrightsorg and more than 100 of our coalition members &amp; partners opposed the bill because it excluded sentencing reform &amp; abandoned years of painstaking, bipartisan efforts to construct a comprehensive reform package.
Bringing fairness and dignity to our justice system is one of the most important civil and human rights issues of our time. But we need to be clear about this: The #FirstStepAct is just that ‚Äì a good first step. There‚Äôs so much more work to do to fix our justice system. Thread:

This could cause hundreds of thousands of people in our communities to avoid the #2020Census out of a real concern of being targeted by this president. 10/
To be clear, asking every household and every person in the country about their citizenship status in the current political environment will contribute to the climate of fear ‚Äì particularly when there's no legal basis to do so. 9/
Beyond legal objections, this unnecessary question will cause panic and alarm. It's unnecessarily intrusive and will raise concerns in all households not only about the confidentiality of information provided to the government ‚Äì but also how government authorities may use it. 8/
Estimates of the citizen voting-age population derived from the ongoing American Community Survey, and the census ‚Äúlong‚Äù form before that, have been more than sufficient for civil rights and Voting Rights Act enforcement. 7/
Since enactment of the Voting Rights Act in 1965, the census has not included a question on citizenship on the form sent to all households ‚Äì which means that this data has never been necessary to enforce our civil and voting rights laws. 6/
But more importantly, their argument is factually incorrect, morally bankrupt, and legally wrong. The Justice Department does not need this question to enforce civil rights protections or the Voting Rights Act. 5/
One, this administration has been downright hostile to Voting Rights Act protections specifically, and civil rights overall. So it‚Äôs laughable to think they suddenly found religion on protecting voting rights now. 4/
As someone who had the specific responsibility of enforcing the Voting Rights Act, I find this argument incredible for two reasons. 3/
We know how others in the Trump administration and Trump Campaign would answer this question. In their letter to @CommerceGov, Trump Justice Department officials claimed that this citizenship question is necessary to enforce the Voting Rights Act. 2/
